  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_dfc04c18-0131-4ab1-9e65-df964f66e6a6'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer1458264077998674752">Princess Lira is siren royalty and the most lethal of them all. With the hearts of seventeen princes in her collection, she is revered across the sea.   <span id="freeText1458264077998674752" style="display:none">Princess Lira is siren royalty and the most lethal of them all. With the hearts of seventeen princes in her collection, she is revered across the sea. Until a twist of fate forces her to kill one of her own. To punish her daughter, the Sea Queen transforms Lira into the one thing they loathe most—a human. Robbed of her song, Lira has until the winter solstice to deliver Prince Elian’s heart to the Sea Queen or remain a human forever.<br /><br />The ocean is the only place Prince Elian calls home, even though he is heir to the most powerful kingdom in the world. Hunting sirens is more than an unsavory hobby—it’s his calling. When he rescues a drowning woman in the ocean, she’s more than what she appears. She promises to help him find the key to destroying all of sirenkind for good—But can he trust her? And just how many deals will Elian have to barter to eliminate mankind’s greatest enemy?</span>
  <a data-text-id="1458264077998674752" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2317673486" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5702679135112239452">Meet our two main characters--<br/><blockquote><b>Lira:</b> <i>In one move, I plunge my fist into the prince’s chest and pull out his heart.</i><br/><br/><b>Elian:</b> <i>Technically, I’m a murderer, but I like to think that’s one of my better qualities.</i></blockquote><br/>That should give you a sense of what to expect. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34499221.To_Kill_a_Kingdom' title='To Kill a Kingdom by Alexandra Christo' rel='nofollow noopener'>To Kill a Kingdom</a> is a <b>pretty dark fantasy for YA</b> and it tells a compelling, vicious story without falling into all the usual tropes. I was pleasantly surprised.<br/><br/>Lira is a siren princess, daughter of the Sea Queen, and known amongst humans as Princes</span>
  <span id="freeText5702679135112239452" style="display:none">Meet our two main characters--<br /><blockquote><b>Lira:</b> <i>In one move, I plunge my fist into the prince’s chest and pull out his heart.</i><br /><br /><b>Elian:</b> <i>Technically, I’m a murderer, but I like to think that’s one of my better qualities.</i></blockquote><br />That should give you a sense of what to expect. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34499221.To_Kill_a_Kingdom" title="To Kill a Kingdom by Alexandra Christo" rel="nofollow noopener">To Kill a Kingdom</a> is a <b>pretty dark fantasy for YA</b> and it tells a compelling, vicious story without falling into all the usual tropes. I was pleasantly surprised.<br /><br />Lira is a siren princess, daughter of the Sea Queen, and known amongst humans as Princes' Bane - because of all the princes whose hearts she has ripped from their chests. I mean it literally; not talking romantics here. When she disobeys her mother, the Sea Queen punishes Lira by turning her into a human. Floating out on the sea with her new pair of legs, Lira is picked up by Prince Elian's ship.<br /><br />Elian is a siren killer and adventurer. He does not want to be bound to the throne he is set to inherit. What he wants more than anything is to put a stop to the Princes' Bane. When it seems like an old fairy tale might hold the secret to finding the Crystal of Keto - and putting a stop to the Sea Queen and her sirens forever - Elian sets out on a perilous journey to uncover it.<br /><br />These two unlikely companions are thrown together by their strange circumstances. Each wants to kill the other but only Lira is aware of both of their identities. I really enjoyed the developing relationship between them that grew through sarcasm-laced banter. Both are somewhat morally questionable and Lira is a murderous anti-heroine bordering on straight-up villain. There's also a band of lovable and funny secondary characters onboard ship.<br /><blockquote>
  <i>“That’s the thing about risks,” Kye says. “it’s impossible to know which ones are worth it until it’s too late.”</i>
</blockquote><br />A romance grows but it is <b>extremely slow burn</b>. I would not recommend this book for readers who like their fantasy heavy on the romance. And, despite the obvious parallels that can be drawn with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/132391.The_Little_Mermaid" title="The Little Mermaid by Hans Christian Andersen" rel="nofollow noopener">The Little Mermaid</a> (Lira loses her siren song instead of her voice), I wouldn't recommend this for those looking for a retelling either. It's very different, and this "mermaid" definitely doesn't want to be human and bag a prince - unless by that you mean killing him. This prince is far more badass, too. <br /><br />There's lots I like here: anti-heroines, slow-burn romance, fairy tales that contain prophecies, fun banter and strong friendships. I only hope I don't get burned out on this influx of sea fantasies after I read my arcs of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36502054.Sea_Witch" title="Sea Witch by Sarah Henning" rel="nofollow noopener">Sea Witch</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29422091.These_Rebel_Waves__Stream_Raiders___1_" title="These Rebel Waves (Stream Raiders, #1) by Sara Raasch" rel="nofollow noopener">These Rebel Waves</a>.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5702679135112239452" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2132879483" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12715853408259452201">Oh my gosh. Oh my gosh. <br/><br/>I am just sitting here in shock and full of feels and alskfjal;skdjfa;lksjf GO ORDER THIS BOOK RIGHT NOW. How am I supposed to write a coherent review? Gah! <br/><br/>Okay *breathes*<br/><br/>So if you haven't seen the description, this is somewhat of a little mermaid retelling, except it has a totally unique spin, pulling in other folklore as well! (Hint: Midas!)<br/><br/>Lira is a siren known as the 'Prince's Bane' - and she's infamous for killing princes. Yep, that's what she does. She rips out the</span>
  <span id="freeText12715853408259452201" style="display:none">Oh my gosh. Oh my gosh. <br /><br />I am just sitting here in shock and full of feels and alskfjal;skdjfa;lksjf GO ORDER THIS BOOK RIGHT NOW. How am I supposed to write a coherent review? Gah! <br /><br />Okay *breathes*<br /><br />So if you haven't seen the description, this is somewhat of a little mermaid retelling, except it has a totally unique spin, pulling in other folklore as well! (Hint: Midas!)<br /><br />Lira is a siren known as the 'Prince's Bane' - and she's infamous for killing princes. Yep, that's what she does. She rips out their hearts. Not to mention, she's the daughter of the mighty Sea Queen who is pretty much terrible all around. She's Ursula if Ursula was chewed up and spit out by the devil himself (but still manages to be attractive). Basically she's the reason Lira is the way she is - and her story is actually quite sad.<br /><br />Annnyyywayyy, Lira is unashamedly brutal and hunts with vicious intent.<br /><br />Elian is a prince whos pastime is piracy. Yep, you heard me. We have a pirate prince on our hands, ladies and gentlemen. Nikolai Lantsov, meet your brother from another mother. Anyway, Elian is hilariously sassy and all around amazing. But why does he patrol the seas, you ask? <br /><br />He hunts sirens. And he kills a great deal of them. <br /><br />So we have a prince killer and a siren killer - the makings of a perfectly delicious story. <br /><br />Anyway, after an event that royally pisses of the Sea Queen, she changes Lira into a human as punishment and orders her to go kill the siren-killer prince (but without her siren powers). Elian finds Lira, who looks like an ordinary girl at this point, conveniently drowning in the ocean. But instead of trying to kill him right off the bat, Lira has another idea - and decides to stick around for a while.<br /><br />That's all I'm going to say.<br /><br />Here's what you need to know:<br /><br />Elian is everything. His crew is everything. The WRITING is everything. (Seriously, all aspiring authors need to read this and revel in its beauty. I have SO MANY LINES highlighted.) There's romance, banter, pirates, action, drama, adventure, strong character arcs, and lots of fun kingdoms. I don't want to spoil anything else. Just read it.<br /><br />Alexandra is a master of creative writing, character, and storytelling. I honestly loved every bit of this book, and you can bet I'll be shoving it at everyone I know. <br /><br /><br /><a href="http://www.herbookishthings.com" rel="nofollow noopener">My Blog</a> ~ <a href="https://www.instagram.com/reverieandink/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> ~ <a href="https://twitter.com/reverieandink" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> ~ <a href="https://www.etsy.com/shop/reverieandink" rel="nofollow noopener">Etsy</a></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2461294060" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2848876244891750717">Where would I be, as a person and in society, without the <b>enemies-to-lovers trope</b> where two people, who are actual literal enemies fighting on opposite sides of a conflict and who can hold their own against each other and even in their hatred have a begrudging respect for the other, come together on equal ground and slowly realize that they have more in common than they’d first thought, they don’t instantly get along but bicker and deny and fight their way into a tentative friendship that is bor</span>
  <span id="freeText2848876244891750717" style="display:none">Where would I be, as a person and in society, without the <b>enemies-to-lovers trope</b> where two people, who are actual literal enemies fighting on opposite sides of a conflict and who can hold their own against each other and even in their hatred have a begrudging respect for the other, come together on equal ground and slowly realize that they have more in common than they’d first thought, they don’t instantly get along but bicker and deny and fight their way into a tentative friendship that is born of a deep understanding and trust and respect found in companionship which later slowly blossoms into a whirlwind of a romance, and the best part? THESE IDIOTS WILL STILL BE ACTING LIKE JACKASSES TO EACH OTHER BUT AFFECTIONATELY AND WITH SO MUCH LOVE!!!<br /><br />Can I just scream about this trope for the rest of my life and let that be my career?<br /><br /><blockquote>☆ <a href="https://ko-fi.com/givemeabrekk" rel="nofollow noopener">ko-fi</a> ★ <a href="https://bookswithchaima.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">blog</a> ☆ <a href="https://twitter.com/givemeabrekk" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a> ★ <a href="https://azqaban.tumblr.com" rel="nofollow noopener">tumblr</a> ☆</blockquote></span>

<div id="review_2414601790" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2414601790" />
    <a title="emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32879029-emma"><img alt="emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520568130p2/32879029.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2414601790?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="emma" href="/user/show/32879029-emma">emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=couldn-t-wait-to-read">couldn-t-wait-to-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=unpopular-opinion">unpopular-opinion</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=nope">nope</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=comments">comments</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32879029-emma?shelf=fairytale">fairytale</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2414601790" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11956940068797309877">This review was discussed on the <a href='http://heygoodbookinpodcast.com/2019/01/27/novellasode-9-dear-twilight-donald-trmp-says-youre-wrong/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hey Good Bookin' podcast</a>! I have never felt cooler.<br/><br/>------<br/><br/>I am proposing a new law: Books that are not good should not be allowed to have really good opening lines. Because then I open them in Barnes & Noble and am like “wow I should buy this” and then I do (except not immediately because I don’t have B&N levels of money honey) and then I’m disappointed and I hate it and it’s honestly bad for all of us.<br/><br/>This law is for the good of the people, you know?<br/><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2018/11/15/universally-loved-books-i-hate-more-unpopular-opinions/'>https://emmar</a></span>
  <span id="freeText11956940068797309877" style="display:none">This review was discussed on the <a href="http://heygoodbookinpodcast.com/2019/01/27/novellasode-9-dear-twilight-donald-trmp-says-youre-wrong/" rel="nofollow noopener">Hey Good Bookin' podcast</a>! I have never felt cooler.<br /><br />------<br /><br />I am proposing a new law: Books that are not good should not be allowed to have really good opening lines. Because then I open them in Barnes &amp; Noble and am like “wow I should buy this” and then I do (except not immediately because I don’t have B&amp;N levels of money honey) and then I’m disappointed and I hate it and it’s honestly bad for all of us.<br /><br />This law is for the good of the people, you know?<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2018/11/15/universally-loved-books-i-hate-more-unpopular-opinions/">https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br /><br />LISTEN TO THIS OPENING LINE YOU GUYS. And by listen to I of course mean read. But like, come on: <i> “I have a heart for every year I’ve been alive.”</i><br /><br />Tell me that doesn’t seem like the rest of the hundreds of pages that follow it should be good!! Tell me! You’d be wrong. It seems like they should be good and yet they aren’t and that is an injustice so massive I will dedicate the rest of my life to getting legislation on the books that will prevent it from ever happening again.<br /><br />Hahahaha. “Legislation on the books.” Get it? Like that’s what you say about passing legislation successfully, but also it would be legislation on books? God I’m funny.<br /><br />But let’s talk synopsis. To Kill a Kingdom is (allegedly) a high fantasy about this gal Lira. Lira’s a siren - the princess of the sirens. Sirens RIP the HEARTS out of dudes!! Pretty rad stuff, violent af, we love it. Lira is especially badass, and she ONLY steals the hearts of princes. F*ck the system, girl, I get it. Take down the patriarchy/our capitalist oppressors/etc etc. I’m still into it.<br /><br />Here’s where you lose me.<br /><br />This is a Little Mermaid retelling (okay actually still rad) in which Lira is given human legs because she takes a heart without it being her birthday (she can only take a heart for every year yadda yadda) and her mom (the queen, a Very Bad Lady) says oh you think you’re so tough??? Okay. Get me the heart of an Extra Special Prince - the Siren Killer.<br /><br />Dun dun dun!<br /><br />This might sound good, unless you’re like me and cynical and well-versed in YA and you know what that actually means. Because if you guessed “Lira will now participate in a not-so-slow burn but absolutely teeming with sh*tty banter romance with the Siren Killer himself, Elian,” you’re today’s lucky winner! Congratulations. Your prize is universal suffering.<br /><br />This should have been violence and revenge and piracy and maybe some cool monarchical world-building if there’s time. Instead, it was boring and romance and boring and terrible banter and boring and confusing info dumps and boring and weird flat writing and oh my god you guys this book was so f*cking BORING!!!<br /><br />I hated this book!!! It’s been so long since I’ve read garbage YA fantasy that I almost forgot why I don’t read YA fantasy like ever!!! Contemporaries can be worse than fantasy could ever be but they are never so horrible to read. <br /><br />Like, let’s talk about the basic requirements of high fantasy that this book does not even BEGIN to satisfy. For one, language??? It’s not that hard to not use slang!! And like I’m SO sorry but when you’re pretending you’re writing high fantasy while using the word “okay” it doesn’t work for me again I’m SO sorry. <br /><br />And if you’re going to write a standalone about a world with one hundred separate island kingdoms and do this bad of a job worldbuilding, honestly please at least give me a map so I can gaze lovingly at it and pretend to enjoy it. This world could have been so cool but we get basically zero geographical or historical or general information, just weird random details about specific island-nations, and I’m quite seriously sick of it!!!<br /><br />I hated the romance. It was mostly banter that was just uniquely terrible, really just a whole new level of unfunny and bad but with characters being like “Wow...she is very funny...I quite like her...ha ha dare I say she is one of the gang...lol you may have met your match, dear sir...sounds like someone else I know...ha ha ha, I kid, oh yes, we have fun, lmao.” <br /><br />Also as established, the language is like one step above using text abbreviations anyway.<br /><br />Anyway once we get past the banter stage of the romance, we jump straight into “icky gross touchy feely lovey dovey I hate it get it away from me.” And then betrayal, and then more of that again! It’s painful in a hundred different ways and it never gets better.<br /><br />Part of this is because THE CHARACTERS ARE AWFUL!!! Lira is nowhere near the cool violent siren I EXPECTED and DESERVED. She’s just mean and prissy and thinks she’s really funny and badass but god she is not at all. <a href="https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2018/05/22/books-everyone-liked-and-i-did-not-more-unpopular-opinions/" rel="nofollow noopener">A lot like another red-haired fishy nemesis of mine.</a><br /><br />And Elian is just...boring. The siren song of the YA male love interest. A real poor little rich boy type situation. SO SORRY YOU MIGHT HAVE TO RULE OVER AN ISLAND MADE OF GOLD, ASSHOLE. WE WEEP FOR YOUR SUFFERING, WE REALLY DO.<br /><br />Speaking of boring, this sh*t had absolutely no right to be and yet here we are. This is the most boring book in the history of ever. I don’t get it! The world-building was god awful, half the characters were flat, there was no setup or explanation or exposition of any kind, and yet NOTHING HAPPENS IN THE FIRST HALF OF THE BOOK. I got halfway through and thought I was only a fraction of the way in! Nope, just bad writing!<br /><br />How do you pitch a violent siren/pirate high fantasy YA retelling of the Little Mermaid and somehow make it boring? That’s almost so awful it turns in on itself and becomes impressive.<br /><br />Almost.<br /><br />Plus this wasn’t violence-y anyway. It was just “““character development.””” Elian spends half the book crying about how it’s so mean of him to kill sirens (they’re only killing his people for no reason, guys!) and Lira spends half the book thinking about how it’s too mean of her to kill someone as <s>sexy</s> great as Elian even though she should be planning that grand revenge plot on her mom she swears is happening and will def involve murder for sure.<br /><br />We get no violence. We get pondering and crying and more pondering and the ultimate condemnation of violence and it is a hundred thousand million times worse than if this were a straightforward Little Mermaid retelling with no violence at all.<br /><br /><b>Bottom line</b>: Boring. Bad characters. Bad romance. Bad world-building. Weird bad writing. Bad, inaccurate synopsis. Boring boring boring, bad bad bad. <br /><br />--------<br /><i>pre-review</i><br /><br />Really starting to think you guys all just pretended this book was good and got me all excited to read it as some sort of elaborate, cruel prank.<br /><br />IT WAS BAD AND NOW I'M DISAPPOINTED.<br /><br />review to come once I recover from this (read: NEVER. I'LL NEVER GET OVER IT)<br /><br />--------<br /><i>currently-reading updates</i><br /><br />I hadn't picked up this book in a couple days and assumed I was like 1/4 of the way into it, since nothing has really happened yet.<br /><br />NOPE.<br /><br />I'M MORE THAN HALFWAY DONE.<br /><br />WHEN ARE WE GOING TO GET TO THE GOOD STUFF.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11956940068797309877" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2272753660" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2272753660" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2272753660?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=2018-reads">2018-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=retellings">retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2272753660" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8733767853108305867"><b>Dark, seductive and oh so beautiful.</b><br/><br/>Dark as a stormy night.<br/>Seductive as the call of a siren.<br/>Beautiful like the bluest sea.<br/>I marvel at how wonderful most of the 2018 YA releases have been. Even though the time I dedicate to reading is far less than what my heart desires (thank you adult life, really), discovering books that sing their melodies to my soul and enchant me to oblivion is a fair compensation. Reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34499221.To_Kill_a_Kingdom' title='To Kill a Kingdom by Alexandra Christo' rel='nofollow noopener'>To Kill a Kingdom</a> was last week's highlight. A <b>blessing</b>. It was <b>a retelling of the Li</b></span>
  <span id="freeText8733767853108305867" style="display:none"><b>Dark, seductive and oh so beautiful.</b><br><br>Dark as a stormy night.<br>Seductive as the call of a siren.<br>Beautiful like the bluest sea.<br>I marvel at how wonderful most of the 2018 YA releases have been. Even though the time I dedicate to reading is far less than what my heart desires (thank you adult life, really), discovering books that sing their melodies to my soul and enchant me to oblivion is a fair compensation. Reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34499221.To_Kill_a_Kingdom" title="To Kill a Kingdom by Alexandra Christo" rel="nofollow noopener">To Kill a Kingdom</a> was last week's highlight. A <b>blessing</b>. It was <b>a retelling of the Little Mermaid made of foam, blood and stars</b>. So, I simply <b>devoured</b> it. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1521905850ra/25268140.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>“I’ ve made a mistake. It started with a prince, as most stories do.”</b>
</blockquote><br>But <b>Elian</b> is not a prince like the others. He's a <b>pirate</b> at heart, and the only place he feels at home is the ocean and his war ship. His kingdom and his responsibilities suffocate him, and so he roams the seas, hunting sirens and making the seas a safer place. <b>Lira</b>, on the other hand, is the daughter of the Sea Queen, known as the <b>Prince's Bane</b>. Each year she harvests a prince's heart on her birthday, as a way to prove her ruthlessness to her cruel mother and secure the loyalty of her future subjects. Monstrous and inhumanly beautiful, the sirens only exist for power, and every other feeling is considered weakness. Until the Prince's Bane and the Siren Hunter cross paths. An unpredictable turn of events brings the Sea Queen's wrath upon Lira, and she ends up exiled, having two legs instead of a tail, and an order to rip the heart out of Elian's still warm body. Elian wants to exterminate the sirens and their Queen. Lira wants to take the throne that belongs to her. In order to achieve their goals, the two sworn enemies need each other. Until the final confrontation, that will probably end with one of them dead. Which one, well that is the question.<br><blockquote>
  <b>“So many hearts. You'll soon run out of room to bury them all.”<br>“Maybe. But a princess must have her prince.”</b>
</blockquote><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34499221.To_Kill_a_Kingdom" title="To Kill a Kingdom by Alexandra Christo" rel="nofollow noopener">To Kill a Kingdom</a> is <b> a dark and slightly twisted fairytale</b>. During the first half of the book, I couldn't shake the notion that it's not a typical story about the prince saving the princess, or vice-versa. Lira and Elian were both <b>anti-heroes</b>, two souls who seemed beneath salvation. Lira begins her narration stating nonchalantly that she collects the hearts of princes, while Elian claims that he's a murderer, and that's not his worst trait. Their hands are stained with blood, something they do not crave, but accept nonetheless. But as the story progressed, something cracked inside of them, and thus inside of me. Lira tasted freedom for the first time in her tragic life, she tasted humanity, and compassion she could not comprehend. Elian found himself trusting this venomous girl with the secrets, and somewhere along the way realised that maybe death is not the only way. In the end, I came to the conclusion that no, it was not a story of anti-heroes. <b>It was the story of the forging of two heroes</b>. <br><blockquote>
  <b>“Be the queen we need you to be. ”</b>
</blockquote><br>I can't pinpoint the exact moment I fell in love with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34499221.To_Kill_a_Kingdom" title="To Kill a Kingdom by Alexandra Christo" rel="nofollow noopener">To Kill a Kingdom</a>. Maybe it happened during the very first chapter, maybe halfway through. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14684499.Alexandra_Christo" title="Alexandra Christo" rel="nofollow noopener">Alexandra Christo</a> has the uncanny ability of bringing characters and objects alike to life. My feelings are like the surface of the sea, calm and then tumultuous, and then peaceful once more. <b>My mind is soaked with images and senses.</b> I can taste licorice in my tongue, and inhale the salty air. I can see the deck of an enormous ship where a siren seethes and turns to foam. Two lonely figures gazing at the stars. A song that speaks of undying love and devotion. Black tentacles scraping skin, and evil laughter that pierces my bones. A sea named after the Devil with the colour of sapphires. Every description was <b>heartbreakingly beautiful</b>, and there was something in the narration that made me feel that I was sitting next to Elian and Lira, listening to their soft voices while the sun burned my skin and the cold water licked my feet. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14684499.Alexandra_Christo" title="Alexandra Christo" rel="nofollow noopener">Alexandra Christo</a>'s prose was <b>magical</b>, her world-building simple yet full of imagination; her lores were entrancing, and her world pulsated with monsters and monstrous humans, brutality and violence, but also a fiery need to belong, to be the person you want to be instead of the one that was forced on you. <br><blockquote>
  <b>“In my heart, I’m as wild as the ocean that raised me.” </b>
</blockquote><br><b>The story of Elian and Lira was pure magic</b>. Two enemies bred in blood, two souls burdened by expectations and invinsible chains, they forged an unwanted alliance, unaware that they would both change in a way they never predicted. There were no flowers and sonnets and love declarations. There were <b>insults, betrayal, lies and deception</b>, that tethered their souls nonetheless. Love didn't make them mushy. It made them strong, and they emerged from their trials better, wiser, more complete.<br><blockquote>
  <b>“He has eyes like vast pools and a jaw made from shipwrecks and broken coral. Every movement he makes is as quick and fluid as a tidal wave. He belongs to the ocean. He is made from it, as much as I am.” </b>
</blockquote><br><b>Hearts are at stake in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/34499221.To_Kill_a_Kingdom" title="To Kill a Kingdom by Alexandra Christo" rel="nofollow noopener">To Kill a Kingdom</a>, a mesmerizing, deeply enthralling story about power, freedom and love. I can't recommend it highly enough!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1521911123ra/25268532.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>P.S. My only complaint is technical. <i>Psàriin</i>, the language of sea, is basically Greek. Being my native language, I have to point out that, even though the use of individual words was correct (and I felt really proud because that doesn't happen quite frequently), the sentences had some issues, and to a person speaking Greek they sounded funny. That's all folks!<br><br><a href="http://booknest.eu/reviews/kat/1096-tokillakingdom" rel="nofollow noopener">BookNest</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/katerina_papas/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8733767853108305867" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2217639862" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2217639862" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2217639862?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/36120821-to-kill-a-kingdom">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2217639862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17135950689333519971"><i>”You are a little heartless today, aren’t you?”<br/>“Never,” I say. “There are seventeen under my bed.”</i> <br/><br/>I asked for a blood thirsty, dark and twisted siren that lures princes and collects their still warm and dripping hearts. And I wanted a strong human prince that hunts wicked sirens and sea witches for sport. Well, I guess <b>“To Kill a Kingdom”</b> did a great job at delivering all this and even more. ;-P<br/><br/> <i>”Technically, I’m a murderer, but I like to think that’s one of my better qualities.”</i><br/><br/>I went into thi</span>
  <span id="freeText17135950689333519971" style="display:none"><i>”You are a little heartless today, aren’t you?”<br />“Never,” I say. “There are seventeen under my bed.”</i> <br /><br />I asked for a blood thirsty, dark and twisted siren that lures princes and collects their still warm and dripping hearts. And I wanted a strong human prince that hunts wicked sirens and sea witches for sport. Well, I guess <b>“To Kill a Kingdom”</b> did a great job at delivering all this and even more. ;-P<br /><br /> <i>”Technically, I’m a murderer, but I like to think that’s one of my better qualities.”</i><br /><br />I went into this book expecting a fast and enjoyable read and if you’re looking for a story like that this book definitely is the right choice for you. I know the reviews for this are about 50:50 when it comes to the ratings but I think that’s mostly due to the expectations you have when you go into a book. If you’re looking for a mind-blowing reading experience you might be disappointed because this story is a lot of things but certainly nothing that will cause you to rethink your life choices. It’s fun, it’s easy, it has plenty of snark, banter and a really great character cast. In short it has everything you need when you want to escape your own world for a little while. <br /><br /><i>”Lies aren’t answers.”<br />“But they sound so much better than the truth.”</i><br /><br />This said I really liked our two MCs and I was a huge fan of their interactions. Those two were both confident in their own skin and it was really refreshing to have two characters that know exactly what they want. Lira wants Elian’s heart and Elian wants to destroy all sirens. The best makings of a good partnership, right? XD Well, almost! If their attraction wouldn’t have gotten into their way things certainly might have been a lot easier. ;-) But I AM a sucker for the “enemies to lovers trope” and it was done really nicely in here so I have nothing to complain about. *lol*<br /><br /><i>”They’re eyes of lost innocence, greener than seaweed and constantly searching. Even the empty ocean is prey to him, and he regards it with a mix of suspicion and wonder.”</i><br /><br />Prince Elian was quite something and to me he was the perfect embodiment of a lost boy. There was no way I wouldn’t love him and his easy nature as well as his love for his crew and ship immediately made him my favourite. Yes, I admit it, I’m a sucker for handsome, sassy and broken <s>pirate</s> boys. They are as much my kryptonite as redheads are so I wasn’t really surprised I ended up liking him so much. Lira on the other hand was pretty awesome too! That girl might have been turned into a human but that did nothing to disguise the feral and deadly siren inside of her. And this brings me to another thing I really enjoyed about this book: Lira and Elian might have been deadly enemies but they still had mutual respect for each other and acknowledged their weaknesses and strengths. <br /><br /><i>”How wicked this one is, stripped of the innocence I’ve seen in all the others. This is not a prince of inexperience and anxious potential, but one of war and savagery. His heart will be a wonder to behold.”</i><br /><br /><i>”I could have killed her, but I didn’t, because she’s a wonder. A creature that has eluded me for so long and then, finally, appeared. Let me be privy to a face few men live to speak about.”</i><br /><br />They were fascinated with each other and it showed throughout the entire book. Also can we take a second to appreciate how self-aware they were? Both of them knew exactly what they were capable of and where they would draw the line and even though they questioned themselves and their own decisions they always knew who they were. And the banter!!! Did I already mention the delicious sarcasm and banter? *lol*<br /><br /><i>”Lira,” I say. “I don’t suppose you’d be kind enough to translate?”<br />“I’ve never been accused of kindness before.”</i><br /><br /><i>”What would you be losing?” he asks.<br />“If I married you?” I stand to tower above him, pushing away the unraveling thing inside me. “I suppose it would be my mind.”</i><br /><br />I loved that they didn’t give each other an inch. They were equals and it wasn’t only easy to see but also palpable. I don’t know how to describe this but there are a lot of books out there that make it seem like the couples in them are equipollent when in fact they are not. Even with kick-ass heroines the male MCs are always stronger somehow. It’s something I noticed in many books and I hate that those amazing women can’t stand on their own feet once they fall in love with their “true love”. It’s something that didn’t happen in here and I was very grateful for it! Lira might have fallen in love with Elian but that didn’t make her go all mushy and lovey-dovey. In fact it only made her even more adamant and relentless, which was <b>AWESOME</b> to behold! XD<br /><br />All told “To Kill a Kingdom” was exactly the kind of quick and entertaining reading experience I needed and I’m glad I finally decided to give it a shot. It took me long enough to get here but it definitely was worth the wait. And just in case you wondered: Yes, I rediscovered my love for “Ariel – The Little Mermaid” once again. *hums under the sea and leaves the room* ;-P<br /><br />______________________________<br /><br />Okay, that ending was kinda wild! *lol*<br />But the story was really great and I loved the new spin on it! <br /><br />Elian and Lira were exactly how I expected them to be and after reading this I think I’ll be able to enjoy “The Little Mermaid” once again. XD<br /><br />Full RTC soon! Stay tuned! This was a fun ride! ;-P<br />_______________________________<br /><br />After listening to <b>“Ariel – The Little Mermaid”</b> for weeks because my little kid loves her, and after singing “Under the Sea” for about the thousandth time I’m finally ready to tackle “To Kill a Kingdom”! *lol*<br /><br />I need a dark and twisted siren that lures princes and <s>eats</s> collects their bloody hearts! <br />And I need a strong human prince that can’t be fooled by her and hunts wicked sea witches for sport. <br /><br />Yep, that’s exactly what I need right now! <br />A super dark retelling... and then I’ll sing “Under the Sea” with my kid again. With more enthusiasm than ever. ;-P<br /><br />__________________________<br /><br />Can I afford to add another book to my ever growing to-be read pile?<br />No!<br /><br />Am I going to add this awesome book that seems to feature not only a siren but also a handsome pirate prince?<br /><br /><b>ABSO-FREAKING-LUTELY!!!! &lt;333</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="17135950689333519971" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2190284688" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2190284688" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2190284688?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=signed">signed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2190284688" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9775465674730466683"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1522703994i/25313553._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><i>ARC provided by Macmillan in exchange for an honest review.</i><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I’ve made a mistake. It started with a prince, as most stories do. Once I felt the thrum of his heart beneath my fingers, I couldn’t forget it.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>You all, I buddy read this with <b>FOUR</b> of my closest book friends, and we all five starred this amazing story. Please, go treat yourself and preorder this book. Please. Do you like killer sirens? Angsty romance? A+ witty banter? Vivid fighting scenes with mind-blowing imagery? One of t</span>
  <span id="freeText9775465674730466683" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1522703994i/25313553._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>ARC provided by Macmillan in exchange for an honest review.</i><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I’ve made a mistake. It started with a prince, as most stories do. Once I felt the thrum of his heart beneath my fingers, I couldn’t forget it.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>You all, I buddy read this with <b>FOUR</b> of my closest book friends, and we all five starred this amazing story. Please, go treat yourself and preorder this book. Please. Do you like killer sirens? Angsty romance? A+ witty banter? Vivid fighting scenes with mind-blowing imagery? One of the best and strongest protagonists I’ve read about in a long while? And all these things in a standalone? From a debut author? Seriously, we’ve been blessed.<br><br>And I can safely say that there is no better feeling than picking up an ARC that is not exceptionally hyped, and that you’re not expecting anything from really, and you come out absolutely loving it. This was perfection and one of the best reading experiences I’ve had all year. I can’t wait for you all to love this book, too, come March 6th.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I have a heart for every year I’ve been alive.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>This is a magical standalone that surrounds two very different people that are both next in line for two very different crowns:<br><br>➽ <b>Lira</b> - AKA: Prince’s Bane, the most feared siren of all time. She has a collection of seventeen royal hearts. She is also the daughter of Sea Queen, who rules the sea kingdom, Diavolos. Yet, the Sea Queen is abusive, a manipulator, a tyrant, and not willing to relinquish her throne anytime soon for Lira. <br>➽ <b>Elian</b> - AKA: Siren Hunter. He is a royal prince, but also a cutthroat sea captain who sees the world on his ship, <i>The Saad</i>, with his crew. His family rules Midas, the city of gold, and they want nothing more than for him to give up his pirate life and to finally be king. Also, Elian and his entire family are brown-skinned.<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Two kingdoms that come with responsibilities we each have trouble bearing. Him, the shackles of being pinned to one land and one life. Me, trapped in the confines of my mother’s murderous legacy. And the ocean, calling out to us both. A song of freedom and longing.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>In this world, humans fear the sirens that lurk below the water. And under the ocean, sirens are forced to bring back a human heart during the month of their birth and present it for all to see. But our dear Lira has taken to only the hearts of royals. This story is very loosely inspired by <i>The Little Mermaid</i>, therefore, I’m sure you guys can somewhat guess how these two’s paths cross. But after Lira upsets her mother, the Sea Queen wants to find a new way to ridicule and humiliate her, so what better way than to force her to steal the most royal heart of all, but also forcing her to do this task as a human, and while no longer having her siren voice to lure humans towards her.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1519420070ra/25111982.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And what kind of prince in waiting would Elian be if he let this damsel in distress drown in the water? I mean, until he rescues Lira and realizes how much of a damsel in distress she really isn’t. You all, this was some of the best banter I’ve ever read in any book, ever. And you guys know that hate to love romance is the trope that I love more than any other. And this angst? Perfection. These two might honestly end up being my favorite partnership of 2018. From actually laughing out loud, to swooning, to crying, to everything I felt for these two, and all I want is more. <br><br>I was astounded by the worldbuilding and how seamlessly it was crafted and presented. Honestly, this entire story’s imagery was so impressive. The last battle was so visually breathtaking, I feel speechless. The last few chapters were perfection, and I feel so honored that I was able to even experience them. Me and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8034382.J_A_Ironside" rel="nofollow noopener">Jules</a> both were absolutely astonished by that last battle and how visually pleasing it was to the mind. I honestly could picture this being a movie immediately. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1519420166ra/25111984.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And this book tackles some pretty serious topics, too. We see parental/adult abuse, manipulation, and gaslighting in this book a lot. Kids only want to be loved, especially from their parents, and it takes a lot to realize that sometimes the people who are supposed to protect you and unconditionally love you just blatantly don’t. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Love is a word we scarcely hear in the ocean. It exists only in my song and on lips of the princes I’ve killed. And I have never heard it from my mother’s mouth.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>And there is such an important and constant theme of how a new generation can change the world. Which is a message that everyone in The United States should be behind right now. As I’m typing this review, high school kids are changing our world, because the baby boomer generation that’s in office currently think it’s more important to protect assault rifles over innocent kid’s lives. Seriously, these teens, who this book is marketed for, won’t be teens for long. They will be voting, they will activists, and they will be changing the damn world for the better. Do you know how powerful it is for them to have books like this? With themes like this? Seriously, this was probably my favorite thing in this book where there was so much to easily love. <br><br>This story also beautiful emphasizes the importance of found families. Blood is nothing more than blood. The people who choose to unconditionally love you, support you, protect you, those people are your family. Madrid, Kye, Torik, Kahlia, I fell in love with all of the side characters. And this book beautifully depicts how important it is for you to choose who is worthy of your time and love. <br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“How strange that instead of taking his heart, I’m hoping he takes mine.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Overall, this was honestly just a joy to read. The writing was lyrical and beautiful. The world building was fantastic and so impressive, especially for a standalone. The romance was absolutely perfect. Also, my <i>Odyssey</i> loving heart will read any and all books about sirens luring men to their death. I loved being on this adventure and journey alongside Lira and Elian. I absolutely cannot wait to see what Alexandra Christo does next, and this debut novel of hers is one of the best debut novels I’ve ever read. <br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a> <br><br><i>The quotes above were taken from an ARC and are subject to change upon publication.</i><br><br><u>Buddy read with:</u><br>🧜‍♀️ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/8034382.J_A_Ironside" rel="nofollow noopener">Jules</a> at <a href="http://www.jaironside.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">JA Ironside</a><br>🧜‍♀️ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/42780417-wren-wrensreads" rel="nofollow noopener">Wren</a> at <a href="http://www.wrensreads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Fables &amp; Wren</a><br>🧜‍♀️ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/2432645-lilly-lair-of-books" rel="nofollow noopener">Lilly</a> at <a href="https://lairofbooksblog.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Lair of Books</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9775465674730466683" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2365140054" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2365140054" />
    <a title="Warda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30036082-warda"><img alt="Warda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1593385153p2/30036082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2365140054?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Warda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Warda" href="/user/show/30036082-warda">Warda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/37769536-to-kill-a-kingdom">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2365140054" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2149817633858437952">I’m disappointed with how mediocre this was. It’s described as a dark and romantic story. <br/>It was dark at the beginning, then turned into mush. By the way our main characters were introduced, I was expecting some straight-up nastiness and bravado. False advertisement that was because that’s not the tone the story carried on with (but I didn’t mind this too much since there was some introspection our characters were going through). <br/>And the romance was...lacklustre. I mean, did it have to be there?</span>
  <span id="freeText2149817633858437952" style="display:none">I’m disappointed with how mediocre this was. It’s described as a dark and romantic story. <br />It was dark at the beginning, then turned into mush. By the way our main characters were introduced, I was expecting some straight-up nastiness and bravado. False advertisement that was because that’s not the tone the story carried on with (but I didn’t mind this too much since there was some introspection our characters were going through). <br />And the romance was...lacklustre. I mean, did it have to be there? It served no purpose. I felt nothing!<br /><br />I think the only aspect that I appreciated was the Prince and his crew, the bond and witty banter they shared. Plus the similarities Elian and Lira had in terms of them both wanting to desperately escape the shackles that had been forced on them. <br /><br />I wanted that angle of their character to be explored (it was too flimsy!) and wanted more brutality. The ending was annoyingly happy. It probably would’ve felt more satisfying had the initial plot point been carried out. I’m slightly getting over happy endings, particularly in fantasy. Or maybe this wasn’t just well done as it was too dramatic for my taste. <br /><br />It felt and read like the story was being crammed in. It wasn’t necessarily slow at any point. The plot was moving, however it seemed almost too calculated and each aspect of the story was placed accordingly. It didn’t flow, rather it felt too deliberate and purposely steered into a particular direction, i.e. getting the two main characters together. <br />Pointless. <br /><br />There wasn’t enough time for me to grow attached to the characters and world, which is a shame, because it had so much potential. I think this would’ve worked better and read more fulfilling had it been a duology possibly, where then the writing, the characters, the world and plot would’ve been given their due right. <br />I liked it enough though. <br /><br /><br /><b>
  <i>Pre-review.</i>
</b><br />This cost a quid. Naturally, I bought it. I miss me some good ol' fantasy. <br />Book, you better deliver. You have standards to uphold now.<br /><br />LEGGO!! 🏃🏾‍♂️</span>
  <a data-text-id="2149817633858437952" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1995912265" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1995912265" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1995912265?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1995912265" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10006977816750901485"><blockquote>
  <i>I HAVE A HEART for every year I’ve been alive.<br/><br/>There are seventeen hidden in the sand of my bedroom. Every so often, I claw through the shingle, just to check they’re still there. Buried deep and bloody. I count each of them, so I can be sure none were stolen in the night. It’s not such an odd fear to have. Hearts are power, and if there’s one thing my kind craves more than the ocean, it’s power.</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1520446785ra/25177119.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>*insert drooling face here* I can't help it. I'm a wee bit bloodthirsty and I <i>love</i> these types of </span>
  <span id="freeText10006977816750901485" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>I HAVE A HEART for every year I’ve been alive.<br><br>There are seventeen hidden in the sand of my bedroom. Every so often, I claw through the shingle, just to check they’re still there. Buried deep and bloody. I count each of them, so I can be sure none were stolen in the night. It’s not such an odd fear to have. Hearts are power, and if there’s one thing my kind craves more than the ocean, it’s power.</i>
</blockquote><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1520446785ra/25177119.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>*insert drooling face here* I can't help it. I'm a wee bit bloodthirsty and I <i>love</i> these types of heroines. *excited squeal*<br><br>Oh hi, remember me? It’s been a long ass time since I reviewed a YA book because I got sick of all the crappy books, but this book caught my eyes (BECAUSE SIRENS) and holy crap, it’s good!<br><br>This is kind of a <i>Little Mermaid</i> retelling but with sirens, and instead of the main character wanting to get forked (no pun intended), our main character sings and seduces and kills the hapless men that fall into her and her cousins' trap.<blockquote>
  <i>“It’ll enchant them all, but if you lay your focus on one, they’ll fall in love with you so resolutely that even as they drown, they’ll scream of nothing but your beauty.”<br><br>“Normally the enchantment is broken when they start to die,” Kahlia says.</i>
</blockquote>*snickers*<br><br>Our prince isn't a handsome, useless fool, but one whose life is devoted to <i>killing</i> sirens. <blockquote>
  <i>The thrill of it never stops, even when the seas become deadly. Even as I hear the familiar song that strikes my soul and makes me believe in love like it’s the first time. The danger only makes me thirstier.</i>
</blockquote><b>Lira</b>, 17-year old siren princess. Through a mistake, she "saves" Prince <b>Elian</b> and gets turned into a human.<blockquote>
  <i>With a shuddering breath, I look down and see legs. Sickly pale things that are crossed awkwardly beneath me, dotted by bruises. Some in big patches, others like tiny fingerprints. And feet, too, with toes pink from the cold.<br><br>My fins are gone. My mother has damned me. I want to die.</i>
</blockquote>It was a really good book. The setting is beautifully woven and explained so that it doesn't feel like a textbook. The characters are vibrant and fun and likable. There are no longing glances and pained flushes and beating hearts, just a slowly developed friendship and alliance that blossoms. I was entertained.<br><br>This would make a pretty good movie.</span>

<div id="review_2332188840" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2332188840" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2332188840?book_show_action=true">Mar 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Daughter of the Pirate King</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=pirates">pirates</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fairy-tale-retellings">fairy-tale-retellings</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=mermaids">mermaids</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=forbidden-love">forbidden-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=dark">dark</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2332188840" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10665253169281273802">A bewitchingly dark retelling of <i>The Little Mermaid</i>.<br/><br/>In which both the siren princess and human prince want to cut each other’s throats if that’s the last thing they do. <br/><br/>Lovely. My newfound love of dark fairytale retellings—caused by <i>Lost Boy: The True Story of Captain Hook</i>—propelled me to read this book.<br/><br/>How could I ever go back to the innocent Disney tales I read as a child that would make me dream of a boundless future? This is atmospheric to the point that I felt Lira and Elian’s hate for each</span>
  <span id="freeText10665253169281273802" style="display:none">A bewitchingly dark retelling of <i>The Little Mermaid</i>.<br /><br />In which both the siren princess and human prince want to cut each other’s throats if that’s the last thing they do. <br /><br />Lovely. My newfound love of dark fairytale retellings—caused by <i>Lost Boy: The True Story of Captain Hook</i>—propelled me to read this book.<br /><br />How could I ever go back to the innocent Disney tales I read as a child that would make me dream of a boundless future? This is atmospheric to the point that I felt Lira and Elian’s hate for each other in the marrow of my bones.<br /><br />And I loved that. Especially since I found the original prince in <i>The Little Mermaid</i> rather one-dimensional, whereas Elian’s personality is attractive. No wonder his crew is so loyal to him: he’s authoritarian without being tyrannical, smart with a bit of smugness showing through, and as dashing on a ship as inside a palace.<br /><br />But this is very much a debut: the world-building is limited, the action scenes various but short (not enough intensity), the romance pleasant but not romantic, and the Sea Queen the stereotypical mother who can never be pleased because she has high expectations… on crack (so a not-so-surprising version of Ursula).<br /><br />On the other hand, it is a fast-paced addictive story that makes you wish more books about sirens and pirates were published, with characters that constantly do the unexpected. <br /><br />The author seriously needs to work on her fighting scenes, but <i>To Kill a Kingdom</i> is a decent source of entertainment. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="10665253169281273802" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2338341927" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2338341927" />
    <a title="Maria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/77602709-maria"><img alt="Maria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1519184646p2/77602709.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2338341927?book_show_action=true">Jul 04, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria" href="/user/show/77602709-maria">Maria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2338341927" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14905813849382308993"><b>3.7</b>/5 Stars ⭐️ ⭐️ ⭐️ ⭐️<br/><blockquote>“Technically, I’m a murderer, but I like to think that’s one of my better qualities.” </blockquote><br/><br/>This is a very hyped up book. You all know it. You all did it. Everyone is reading it and I just couldn't resist. Fantasy is not the genre I prefer but a book about mythology and sirens and pirates is right up my alley. I truly enjoyed this book, it was a very strong debut novel, but it contained its faults.<br/><br/><i>Princess Lira is siren royalty and the most lethal of them all. With the hearts of</i></span>
  <span id="freeText14905813849382308993" style="display:none"><b>3.7</b>/5 Stars ⭐️ ⭐️ ⭐️ ⭐️<br /><blockquote>“Technically, I’m a murderer, but I like to think that’s one of my better qualities.” </blockquote><br /><br />This is a very hyped up book. You all know it. You all did it. Everyone is reading it and I just couldn't resist. Fantasy is not the genre I prefer but a book about mythology and sirens and pirates is right up my alley. I truly enjoyed this book, it was a very strong debut novel, but it contained its faults.<br /><br /><i>Princess Lira is siren royalty and the most lethal of them all. With the hearts of seventeen princes in her collection, she is revered across the sea. Until a twist of fate forces her to kill one of her own. To punish her daughter, the Sea Queen transforms Lira into the one thing they loathe most--a human. Robbed of her song, Lira has until the winter solstice to deliver Prince Elian's heart to the Sea Queen or remain a human forever. <br /><br />The ocean is the only place Prince Elian calls home, even though he is heir to the most powerful kingdom in the world. Hunting sirens is more than an unsavory hobby--it's his calling. When he rescues a drowning woman in the ocean, she's more than what she appears. She promises to help him find the key to destroying all of sirenkind for good--But can he trust her? And just how many deals will Elian have to barter to eliminate mankind's greatest enemy?</i><br /><br />As I promised to some of you, I will rant about the use of my native language, Greek, in this book. <i> Psariin=🐠 </i>, the language of the sirens is basically Greek. When I started reading this book and read the first Greek word, I was pretty fucking excited. Greek isn't often mentioned in books as far as I'm concerned, though it is mentioned more in film and television. When Greek is used incorrectly in film and television, we don't take it seriously. We have made memes out of badly used Greek in film and television. I'm serious. (Γεια σου καλημέρα, γεια σου καληνύχτα, γεια σου καληνότσες.) But it's different in literature. Literature is serious, mistakes like these I'm about to tell you shouldn't exist. They should have consulted a Greek person about it, it wouldn't be so hard. Even an 8 year old could find the mistakes in these. But I will start with the correct usage of my language. Here are some of the kingdoms with Greek names and their translations in English:<br /><br /><b>Adekaros</b> = <i>Penniless</i><br /><b>Diavolos</b> = <i>Hell</i><br /><b>Armonia</b> = <i>Harmony</i><br /><b>Pagos</b> = <i>Ice</i><br /><b>Kleftes</b> = <i>Thieves</i><br /><b>Kalokairi</b> = <i>Summer</i> (ΟΛΑ ΜΟΙΑΖΟΥΝ ΚΑΛΟΚΑΙΡΙ)<br /><b>Eidyllio</b> = <i>Romance</i><br /><b>Agrios</b> = <i>Rough</i><br /><b>Polemistes</b> = <i>Warriors</i><br /><b>Kardia</b> = <i>Heart</i><br /><b>Glossa</b> = <i>Language</i> (Αυτή είναι η φάση, δεν είναι αυτή η φάση. Σνιφ)<br /><b>Psemata</b> = <i>Lies</i> (ΕΙΠΕΣ ΠΩΣ ΜΕ ΘΕΣ ΨΕΜΑΤΑ)<br /><b>Efevresi</b> = <i>Invention</i><br /><br />These are some of the 100 kingdoms mentioned and described in the book. I will give it to them on that, the descriptions of the kingdoms matched their words amazingly and a translation wasn't particularly needed. Although, it should have been added, anyone could understand what each kingdom was about. The way the words were spelled though was incorrect... a Greek person can pronounce them easily but I doubt someone who doesn't speak Greek at all, can. But let's let this pass.<br /><br />Let's go now to the correct usage of some words and phrases in Greek:<br /><br />p. 35 <b> Dolofonos</b> = <i>Murderer</i>, <b>Choiron</b> = <i>Pig</i> (it's a lighter version of pig, like penis is to dick, for example)<br />p. 103 <b>Aidiastiko gourouni</b> = <i>Disgusting pig</i><br />p. 105 <b>Parakalo</b> = <i>Please</i> (here in Greece we never beg with only parakalo, we say se or sas parakalo, but I will let it slide)<br />p. 190 <b>Porni mou</b>= <i>My whore</i> (this is so funny in Greek, I was laughing my ass off for 2 hours)<br />p. 307 <b>Tha pethanete</b> = <i>You will all die</i><br /><br />Well, nothing to say here. These were correct, not their spelling exactly, but they were correct. Some of these had translations, some of them didn't. I think they all should have been translated. Moving on to my favorite part. The butchering of my language. Here I am, reading my book in silence, minding my own business etc.etc. And then comes the dreaded page 104. This is where the magic happened, not in Diavolos Sea. This is where the memes started happening, this is where I started sending these funny af sentences to my friends. Let's go to the paradise:<br /><br />p. 104 <b>Aschimi ligo skyla</b>. It is supposed to be translated to <i>"filthy little bitch"</i>. If you're not Greek, you won't understand how funny this is. It's like saying "filthy a bit bitch" or something. The correct one is <b>"aschimi mikri skyla"</b>. We don't really say that here, but it's the right translation.<br />p. 104 <b>Tha sas skotoso ton eafto mou</b>. It's like she's saying <i>"I will kill myself"</i>. It's so wrong, I can't even look at it. The correct one would be <b>"tha sas skotoso"</b> = <i>I will kill you myself</i><br />p. 105 <b>Prinkipissa</b>. It's <b>Prigkipissa</b> which means <i>"Princess"</i>.<br />p. 111 <b>Pote den tha</b>. It was supposed to say <i>"I would never"</i> but we don't cut it that way here like in English. It's <b>"pote den tha to ekana"</b>.<br />p. 112 <b>Ego den tha sas prodosei</b>. She's saying <i>"I won't betray you"</i>, but the right usage is <b>"ego den tha sas prodoso"</b>.<br />p. 191 <b>Anthropinos</b>. It says <i>"human"</i> but the word <b>"anthropinos"</b> is the adjective. <b>"Anthropos"</b> is the noun. <br />p. 308 <b>Ilthia anoitos</b>. It's supposed to say <i>"stupid fool"</i> but in Greek it's redundant to use both. So just only say <b>"ilithia"</b> or only <b>"anoiti"</b>.<br />p. 312 <b>Anoitos</b>. Its translation is <i>"fool"</i> and the right usage is <b>"anoite"</b>. <br />p. 312 <b>Parte ton apo ton</b>. Guys, I'm fucking serious, I have no idea what this is supposed to say. It doesn't make any fucking sense! Anyone who knows, comment down below.<br /><br />I find these mistakes inexcusable and sloppy. This is Google Translate guys. It's fucking Google Translate. If I go to Google Translate right now and search these, these will be the results. <i></i>Psariin is the language of the protagonist's people, it's so important in the plot, it's a huge part of the book and it was slaughtered this way. I'm very disappointed. I was so excited to see my language written inside a novel and they did me like this. After a certain point, I couldn't take it seriously. I was just laughing. I'm not an expert on linguistics or anything and there were also some other mistakes I can't explain in English. I also don't know if I forgot some part from the book, I'm sorry about that. Anyone who wants to correct me on anything, feel free. <br /><br />*don't mind the Greek sentences, just some memes and inside jokes for my Greek friends in here to enjoy 😉 <br /><br />Now let's go down to the actual book. Let's start with the writing. ✍️ I adored her writing, She pictured vivid images of the worlds, the dialogue was on point, the characters lovable. The world she created was very rich and beautiful. I loved the mythology, the creatures, the kingdoms. They were all fascinating to me. The politics not so much. But politics always bore me.<br /><br />Second of all, let's talk about the romance. I loved Lira and Elian. They were both amazing characters. Anti-heros who were so alike and yet so different. I think the romance happened a bit fast. I felt like after Elian came back for her, it was instant. It wasn't that obvious and it didn't bother me, but it was there. I shipped it though. I truly did.<br /><br />I will talk about the pace of the book a bit. I felt like certain parts that needed more pages were rushed and the opposite. I felt like the book didn't have the best balance. And also I would like to say something about the other characters, except Elian and Lira. While I loved these two characters with a passion, I don't think the author succeeded as much to make the other characters memorable. They were all lovable, but they were just there for me. Like they only served the purpose of being Elian's true family and they weren't something by themselves. It might be only me, but I don't think I will remember these characters after a while.<br /><br />To sum it all up, this was a thrilling debut. With many mistakes and faults, but the story was enthralling. I will remember it for a long time (mostly because of the Greek lol) but after I remember the butchered Greek, I will remember this beautiful story. So... till the next one K BYE!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14905813849382308993" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
